V. (FRAUNHOFER) / Germany Description of the legal entity  Fraunhofer is the leading organisation for applied research in Europe, undertaking contract research on behalf of industry, the service sector and government. At present, Fraunhofer has about eighty research units, including fifty-seven research institutes, at over forty locations in Germany. An annual turnover of about €900 million is generated by contract research by a staff of about thirteen thousand employees. Fraunhofer’s institute für Verfahrenstechnik und Verpackung (Fraunhofer-IVV) will participate in this project:  Fraunhofer’s Institute for Process Engineering and Packaging (Fraunhofer-IVV) has two hundred and twenty-one employees and an annual turnover of €18 million. The Fraunhofer-IVV develops and optimizes products and processes primarily in the area of food ingredients, functional films, product safety, food quality, biogenic raw materials as well as plastics recycling. The department ‘Recycling polymers’ at Fraunhofer-IVV has been founded in 2005 and deals with the separation of pure polymers from plastic containing waste by means of mechanical pre-treatment and solvent based technologies. The latter have been developed at Fraunhofer-IVV (CreaSolv® Process) and enable the dissolution, separation and recovery of target polymers from complex mixtures. This has been successfully exemplified in number of national and European projects (e.g. POLYSOLVE) dealing with ELV, WEEE and EPS/ETICS from construction waste.  The department ‘Material development’ at Fraunhofer-IVV has started activities in the field of vacuum web coating in 1988 as a neutral R&D partner for industry. Since then, many large projects have been successfully completed and packaging materials for food and non-food applications with constantly-improved functionalities have been developed. With respect to protein based biopolymers, they have optimized processing parameters and a strategy to gain specific fractions with defined purity. They have successfully led the whey formulation work in the WHEYLAYER project. They also have over 20 years experience in coating (lacquering and vacuum coating), extrusion of flexible polymer films and in developing corresponding multilayer structures for flexible packaging with high barrier properties (such projects as TRANSMACH, HIPROLOCO, FLEXONICS, NANOINSULATE, SUNFLOWER, SMARTONICS).  

                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018  
820695- MultiCycle- Part B   Page 65 of 117 
The pilot plants at Fraunhofer-IVV contains all relevant processes, relevant to the development, production of flexible single/multi-layered films and thereby, validation of the application of the recycled plastics for packaging applications. The relevant processes for validation of recycled plastics to be used at Fraunhofer-IVV are film extrusion, vacuum deposition, lacquering application and adhesive lamination of polymer films. Fraunhofer-IVV is specialized on gas and water vapor permeability measurements for food packaging and also for high-end applications. With respect to recycling, our facilities allow trials in extended laboratory and small-technical scale. Main tasks Fraunhofer will lead WP2, in charge of developing suitable solvent based processes for multilayer packaging and fibre reinforced composites. These will be done in the existing CreaSolv® pilot line and purity of recycled polymers will be evaluated in Fraunhofer laboratories using FTIR, DSC and XRF. Furthermore, they will contribute to designing an upscaled pilot plant. This plant will be engineered and built by LOEMI in WP4. As a process inventor Fraunhofer will largely contribute to this work package tasks. The Factory outlet test (T4.3) and demonstration trials (T4.4-4.6) using the new pilot plant wil be organized, performed and reported by Fraunhofer.  Fraunhofer-IVV will also have a strong role in WP5: Demonstration of packaging material production using recycled plastics and identification of their usage for food or non-food packaging applications. Production of single and multi-layered structures by means of extrusion plant and wet-chemical coating unit will be performed from the recycled polymers. The produced packaging materials will be characterised in terms of their functional properties and compared to those of the requirements for various packaging applications. Extrusion, co-extrusion of recycled polymers, lamination of metallized recycled PET to recycled extruded PE or PP layers by means of wet chemical lamination unit, process optimization will be the main tasks. Other tasks are water vapor and gas transmission rate measurements, adhesion strength measurements, layer thickness characterisation, and characterization of packaging materials towards food compliance and assessment reports in comparison to the packaging materials produced by using virgin plastics.  FRAUNHOFER will act as Technical manager of the project. How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project Fraunhofer-IVV has 20 years of experience in solvent based separation of plastic mixtures. Starting with laboratory scale experiments in 1996, the CreaSolv® Process can now separate most thermoplastic materials from complex waste streams and produce recycled polymers with defined virgin-like properties, whereas the applied solvent is recycled within the process completely. Thus, the recycling process encourages the circular economy approach, as most recent project results (e.g. Polysolve) have shown that product qualities of recycled polymers comply with specifications of virgin plastics, enabling a use of recycled plastics in initial applications. Having such a technical recycling concept validated, Fraunhofer-IVV provides expertise in defining and building structures for a circular economy of plastics, composites.  Fraunhofer-IVV has also an experience of more than 20 years in roll-to-roll coating (lacquering and vacuum coating), extrusion of flexible polymer films and in developing corresponding multilayer structures for flexible packaging applications with various functionalities, e.g. gas/water vapor barrier, optical properties, and enhanced adhesion, anti-microbial. Several multi-national projects have been successfully completed funded by the European Commission, such as SUSTAINPACK, WHEYLAYER, ACOSIC BIOBOARD, TRANSMACH, HIPROLOCO, FLEXONICS, OLATRONICS, NANOINSULATE, SUNFLOWER. The flexible multifunctional materials developed in these European projects were for food and non-food packaging applications, for the encapsulation of flexible thin film photovoltaics, for vacuum insulation panels for the building and the construction industry. Fraunhofer-IVV has the required expertise for validation of the recycled polymers for packaging applications; for food and non-food products. Packaging for food and pharmaceuticals is a highly regulated area for both the materials and the production environment. The barrier to entry for new players is thus large. For companies established in this market and research organisations active in this field, the hurdle for new materials is one of testing, data evaluation and documentation. As a packaging institute, Fraunhofer-IVV with specialists at its department of Product Safety and Analytics is very familiar with the EC and USA regulations for the food contact materials sector. The U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) regulates a wide variety of areas such as food and packaging, drugs and packaging, cosmetics, medical devices and most recently, pet food and packaging. The FDA regulates plastics through a number of specific regulations. There is a similar regulatory system in the EU (e.g. EU Packaging and Packaging Waste Directive 94/62/EC limits heavy metal content in packaging materials). Food packaging is covered by the general EU Framework Regulation no.1935/2004 and in particular for plastics by the EU Regulation no.10/2011. Fraunhofer-IVV has an accredited test laboratory (according to DIN EN ISO/IEC 17025), which is equipped for the complete analysis and evaluation of food contact materials for compliance with food legislation. This covers all packaging materials like for example printed and coated polymers, or extruded 
                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018  
820695- MultiCycle- Part B   Page 66 of 117 
plastics. Based on the test and evaluation results, specific actions can be taken for optimization of MultiCycle process for packaging materials. Fraunhofer-IVV can provide technical support to the packaging partner to achieve the objectives of the project. Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment, relevant to the proposed work CreaSolv® pilot plant: Fraunhofer IVV runs a flexible CreaSolv® pilot line consisting of some 100-250 L vessels for different unit operations like dissolution, mechanical cleaning, extractive cleaning, product drying and solvent recovery.   In the past it was used to produce 5-100 kg samples of – amongst others - ABS, PS, PC/ABS, PP, PE, PET and PA. This line has a capacity of 5-10 kg/day and will be the base of design studies deducing optimized process parameters for a 25 kg/h plant. The output of this pilot line are intermediate polymer pellets that are offline transferred to a vacuum extrusion line which is used to parametrize a final drying of intermediate products.  Figure 1. CreaSolv® pilot installation at Fraunhofer -IVV  In MultiCycle, there will be two pilot-plant equipment, which will be used for pre-production runs to evaluate processing parameters and functional properties of recycled polymers for packaging applications:  1) Extrusion plant, 2) Wet chemical coating unit. Fraunhofer-IVV provides facilities for carrying out processing trials on a scale from a minimum of 1 kg up to several 100 kg. These are then optimized for industrial-scale production plants. These plants will allow:  - trials to be conducted using small amounts of materials   

                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018  
820695- MultiCycle- Part B   Page 68 of 117 
- small-batch production runs  - new materials or new material combinations to be tested for their processing and application properties  - optimization of the processing of new materials  - transfer of the recorded process parameters to production plants (e.g. at the packaging project partner AMCOR)  1) Extrusion Plant: Extrusion is the most important process for manufacturing of plastic films. A 5-layer and a 7-layer extrusion plant are available, which can be used to produce a wide range of multi and single-layered materials. Figure 1 below shows the picture of the 7-layer flat film extrusion plant. The extruder is a seven-layer-coextrusion unit for four different polymers. It allows the production of multi-layer film structures, the extrusion of single-layer films and the extrusion coating of film sheets as well. The film thickness is monitored in-line with a capacitive sensor. The main extruder is designed as a test extruder for measuring the pressure in the cylinder. The nozzle width is 300 mm; the width of the film can be adjusted up to 500 mm. The mass throughput is in the 1 kg/h to 15 kg/h range. The film thickness can be varied from 20 μm to 3 mm at processing speeds of up to 16 m/min. Extrusion lamination or extrusion coating is also possible.   Figure 2. 7-layer extrusion plant at Fraunhofer-IVV for the extrusion, co-extrusion of recycled plastic pellets 2) Wet chemical coating unit: A wet chemical coating machine is available, which is unique in its possibilities of applying thin adhesive layers, in drying and curing, and in sensitively treating the barrier layers until lamination (Figure 3).   Figure 3. Coating pilot line at Fraunhofer-IVV for the lamination of the extruded recycled PE-, PET-, and vacuum deposited recycled PET, to be used for packaging applications  Analytics: Fraunhofer-IVV possesses all the necessary analytical equipment for characterizing of recycled materials, model products and their application properties after the production of the packaging materials. The analytical facilities and know-how of the personnel at the Fraunhofer-IVV guarantee objective and expert characterization of recycled materials and after the production of the packaging materials, including the compliance tests for food packaging.  They have equipment for the measurement of humidity and oxygen permeation to the best tolerance levels, rheometer, DSC, Raman, SEM, AFM, mechanical properties. In addition, equipment is available for migration analysis, Headspace-GC and liquid phase chromatography for validation of the recycled plastics use in food packaging.

(ELG) / UK Description of the legal entity  ELG Carbon Fibre has been operating the world's first commercial scale continuous carbon fibre recycling plant since 2009. The site is fully licensed by the UK Environment Agency and has the capacity to process in excess of 2000 metric tons of carbon fibre composite waste each year. ELG owns its manufacturing plant and laboratory. All facilities are on the one site in Wolverhampton. These are independent from any other partners’ equipment. Main tasks ELG will characterise the recycled carbon fibres and will produce a hybrid nonwoven, using its nonwoven laboratory line (purely mechanical process) using the recycled carbon fibres and the recycled thermoplastic fibres (WP3 and 6). In WP4 they will be training on the pilot plant to consider a possible future uptake. ELG will also help with the safety, environmental and economic sustainability assessment, the market strategy and innovation impacts, thanks to its years of experience in the recycling and commercialisation of carbon fibres. How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project ELG Carbon Fibre has a strong expertise in the recycling of carbon fibres and the re use of those recycled fibres. With its team and resources, including product development and technical services engineers, with different areas of expertise (textile, composite, chemistry) the company can carry out full feasibility study, the production of prototypes and their complete characterization. As such they have recently delivered a solution to an American’s cup racing team, which will, thanks to ELG’s work, be able to re-use their waste for the production of the next boat generation. ELG is working under the aerospace quality standard AS9100C and conducts its development work according to this standard. Participant no. 8 Name (short name)/ Country Bond-Laminates (BONDL)/ Germany Description of the legal entity  Bond-Laminates, based in Brilon, Germany, has more than 15 years’ experience in development and manufacturing and its application development of thermoplastic composites. The innovative Tepex® material system of Bond-Laminates supports customized solutions from innovative material and parts design to efficient mass production processing and has already been successfully applied in versatile applications and markets. Material development constantly expands the range of materials and properties to address new application areas with tailored solutions. Tepex® is a high performance composite laminate system made with thermoplastic polymers. The innovative combination of continuous reinforcing fibers with thermoplastic polymers results in exceptionally high strength and rigidity, coupled with extremely low weight. Tepex® enables cost-effective parts fabrication processes suitable for mass-production, especially in combination with injection molding. Due to its versatility and outstanding property profile, Tepex® addresses the megatrends of our time: green mobility, individual properties and design, enhanced safety and durability as well as sustainable solutions for the protection of resources and the environment. Whenever lightweight design, stiffness and strength, fatigue resistance, energy absorption and functional integration are required in high volume, Tepex® is the material of choice. Since 2012, Bond-Laminates belongs to LANXESS AG, a leading specialty chemicals company, as a wholly-owned subsidiary. As a part of the High-Performance Materials business unit, Bond-Laminates complements LANXESS competences in the field of innovative lightweight materials. LANXESS has a market presence of 52 production sites in 29 countries worldwide. In 2015 LANXESS achieved net sales of EUR 7.9 billion with 16,600 employees. The core business of LANXESS is the development, manufacturing and marketing of plastics, intermediates and specialty chemicals. LANXESS is a member of the leading sustainability indices Dow Jones Sustainability Index (DJSI) World and FTSE4Good as well as the Carbon Disclosure Leadership Index (CDLI). Main tasks Bond-Laminates (BONDL) will have a big role in WP2 and WP6 but also chairing the working group on composites. This waste may need to be prepared for transport or converted to a form fitting the subsequent recycling steps. In WP6 Bond-Laminates will implement the recycled polymers into its production processes

Participant no. 11 Name (short name)/ Country GBP Metal Group SL / GBP (Spain) Description of the legal entity  BELLVER PLA GROUP aware of the need of a new paradigm for the use of resources has devoted their main activities to the valorisation; recovery and recycling of scrap metal and as well or other recyclable materials. BELLVER PLA GROUP consists of 4 companies (Bellver Pla, Trans-Recicla, Desguaces Santa Ana and Fragmentadora y Metales) strategically located throughout the province of Valencia and Zaragoza, with over 50 years’ experience in the recycling sector. BELLVER PLA GROUP is an Authorised Treatment Centre of Vehicles and a member of the Spanish Federation of Recycling (FER). When the vehicle reaches the end of their useful life, they get decontaminated and treated at our facilities. Once decontaminated they are then transported and fragmented at the shredder plant that we have in Calatayud, Zaragoza. During the whole process, all relevant paperwork and certificates are issued. BELLVER PLA GROUP has a modern and advanced classification system that allows sorting metals according to their size, as well as the recovery of other material light fractions. In BELLVER PLA GROUP over 200,000 tons of materials, both ferrous and non-ferrous, are treated every year. 

                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018

List of up to 5 relevant publications, and/or products, services (including widely-used datasets or software), or other achievements relevant to the call content  End-of-life vehicles (ELV): BELLVER PLA GROUP is an Authorised Treatment Centre of Vehicles for end of life vehicles collection, management and disposal with respect for the environment. The vehicles are treated in the following four steps: dismantling (security) and depollution, spare parts collection, shredding, treatment of shredder residues.  Recovery and recycling: BELLVER PLA GROUP devotes their main activities to the valorisation; recovery and recycling of scrap materials. After the shredding of ELVs, the following material families can are recovered for further processing or energy recovery: lightweight materials (plastic polymers - 85%, textile fibers - 3%, fine - 10%, metals - 2.5%), mixture of materials with apparent density greater than 0.3 gr./cm3 (metals, rubber, thermoplastic polymers, glass), ferrous materials (small materials - less than 3mm, materials with a density greater than 0.6 gr/cm3, textile materials and rest of materials such plastic polymers, thermoplastic polymers, rubber and PVC wire. All this mixture is sent to detectors with inductive sensors for the selection and segregation.     Participant no. 12 Name (short name)/ Country Amcor Group GmbH / AMCOR (Switzerland) Description of the legal entity  Amcor is a global packaging company with 200 sites in more than 40 countries. The business develops and produces flexible and rigid plastic packaging, with around 95% of sales made to food, beverage, healthcare, and tobacco packaging end markets. Amcor converts raw materials – including polymers, aluminium foil and fibre – into packaging products. At Amcor, we believe in responsible packaging that is better for people, products, and the world around us. Safety and sustainability guide how we do business. Our ongoing efforts to reduce the weight and material used in our packaging, improve efficiency of our production processes, and support recycling initiatives and infrastructure align with those values and our business goals. Amcor is a core partner in the Ellen MacArthur Foundation’s (EMF) New Plastics Economy initiative, a three-year effort to design a plastics value chain based on circular-economy principles, where plastics are intended to be used over and over. Amcor people are applying their packaging knowledge to increase the volume of packaging that can be recycled and reused, better protecting people and the environment. During 2016/17, Amcor began working on pioneering projects to develop a global definition for recycle-ready flexible packaging; evaluate chemical recycling; and map material flows and develop strategies to prevent litter and improve recycling in Asia. Amcor helped to shape and is judging entrants to the EMF’s USD 2 million innovation challenge, which was announced in May 2017. The company is part of the Ocean Conservancy’s Trash Free Seas Alliance to eliminate ocean trash, in conjunction with partners such as Nestlé Waters, Procter & Gamble, the World Wildlife Fund, and Coca-Cola. We encourage and support colleagues who volunteer during the International Coastal Cleanup each September. Through this Alliance, we are driving improved waste management practices worldwide, particularly in Southeast Asia. Amcor participates in Materials Recovery for the Future, the Reflex Consortium, and REDCycle to improve recycling opportunities for flexible film packaging. We are active members in industry bodies, including Aluminium Stewardship Initiative, the European Organization for Packaging and the Environment, Flexible Packaging Association, SAVE FOOD Initiative, and the Sustainable Packaging Coalition. In the 16th year of an ongoing partnership with the Earthwatch Institute, 15 Amcor people participated in a research expedition to Bali, Indonesia. There they observed, collected, and documented marine debris to help researchers identify its source, and to develop approaches to prevent waste from reaching beaches and oceans. The colleagues are also identifying solutions to help improve recyclability efforts. At regional levels, Amcor is a core member of two initiatives aimed at driving development of recycling options for flexible packaging: CEFLEX in Europe (also building on the U.K.-focused REFLEX project) and Materials Recovery for the Future (MRFF) in the United States. Also, in the United States, Amcor continues its involvement with the Recycling Partnership, an industry-funded public/ private program to improve residential recycling rates. In 2016/17, funds were used to implement curbside cart programs in St. Paul, Minnesota; 

                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018

Outagamie County, Wisconsin; and Athens, Ohio. Main tasks Amcor Flexibles EMEA will lead WP5: Demonstration of packaging material production using recycled plastics and identification of their usage for food or non-food packaging applications. Production of single and multi-layered structures by means of extrusion plant, thin film barrier coating and adhesive lamination technology unit will be performed from the recycled polymers. The produced packaging materials will be characterised in terms of their functional properties and compared to those of the requirements for various packaging applications. Extrusion, co-extrusion of recycled polymers, lamination of metallized / SiOx recycled PET to recycled extruded PE or PP layers by means of adhesive lamination unit, process optimization will be the main tasks. Other tasks are water vapor and gas transmission rate measurements, adhesion strength measurements, layer thickness characterisation, and characterization of packaging materials towards food compliance and assessment reports in comparison to the packaging materials produced by using virgin plastics.  Amcor Flexibles EMEA will also have a role in WP2 and 4 by proposing and providing difficult to recycle (with current mechanical recycling technology) flexible packaging samples. Amcor and the Fraunhofer IVV have already selected the following not recycling-ready structures to be evaluated:  OPET/Alu/PE, OPET/OPA/PE, OPET/Alu/PP, PETSiOx/PE, PET/metPET/PE, PET/PE-EVOH-PE, OPA/PE, Coex PA-Tie-PE and Paper/Alu/PE. How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project Amcor is the first global packaging company pledging to develop all its packaging to be recyclable or reusable by 2025, directly addressing a major environmental issue with its capability, scale and reach. At the same time, we have committed to significantly increasing our use of recycled materials and driving consistently more recycling of packaging around the world (https://www.amcor.com/blogs/amcor%E2%80%99s-2025-pledge-a-pivotal-moment-for-sustaina). Amcor has experience is using post-consumer recycled polymers and developed the industry’s first liquid laundry detergent bottle made of 100% post-consumer recycled (PCR) polyethylene terephthalate (PET) resin, the Amcor Method Laundry Detergent Bottle won Diamond awards in the Technological Advancement, Responsible Packaging and Enhanced User Experience categories. Developed by our Rigid Plastics group, this sleek, 53-ounce transparent custom container successfully answered the compatibility and colour stability challenges of using PET in the liquid laundry detergent market.    Amcor has also an extensive experience in extrusion of flexible polymer films and in developing corresponding multilayer structures for flexible packaging applications with various functionalities, e.g. gas/water vapor barrier, optical properties, and enhanced adhesion. Amcor is involved in several multi-national projects like REFLEX, MRFF, CEFLEX, The project Barrier (New Plastic Economy from the Ellen Mac Arthur Foundation). Amcor has the required expertise for validation of the recycled polymers for packaging applications; for food and non-food products. Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment, relevant to the proposed work In MultiCycle, there will be Pilot lines and Analytical Centre of Excellence, which will be used for pre-production runs to evaluate processing parameters and functional properties of recycled polymers for packaging applications. Amcor Centre of Excellence provides facilities for carrying out processing trials on a scale from a minimum of 1 kg to 1 tonne. These are then optimized for industrial-scale production plants. These plants will allow:   trials to be conducted using small amounts of materials    small-batch production runs   recycled materials or recycled material combinations to be tested for their processing and application properties   optimization of the processing of the recycled materials   transfer of the recorded process parameters to production plants 1) Extrusion Centre of Excellence Extrusion is the most important process for manufacturing of plastic films. A mono layer (blown and cast) extrusion pilot line, a 3-layer cast extrusion film pilot line, a 5-layer cast and 5-layer extrusion-coating/lamination pilot lines and a 7-layer blown film pilot line are available, which can be used to produce a wide range of multi and single-layered materials made from recycled polymers through CreaSolv technology. Figure 1a below shows the picture of the mono-layer (blown and cast) extrusion pilot lines 
                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018  
820695- MultiCycle- Part B   Page 88 of 117 
 Figure 1a: Mono-layer (blown and cast) film extrusion pilot lines The mono-layer cast film extrusion pilot line (Brabender) contains of 3 different screws design, 3 heating zones, 5 pressure sensors and 1 melt pump. The width of the film can be adjusted up the 200 mm and the mass throughput from 0.2 to 8 kg/h. Cast extrusion and extrusion-lamination or extrusion-coating are possible. The mono-layer cast / blown film extrusion pilot line (Göttfert) also enable to run a die deposit evaluation, a film quality assessment in term of number of number of gels, black spots and an elongational viscosity curve’s (Rheothens). The width of the film can be adjusted up the 200 mm. Figure 1b below shows the picture of 3 and 5-layers cast film extrusion pilot line  Figure 1b: 3 and 5-layers cast film extrusion pilot line The 3 layers cast film extrusion pilot line (Collin) contains 3 extruders, until 5 layers combining system (ABC and ABCBA) and a 350 mm die width for co-extrusion. The film thickness can be varied from 10 μm to 150 microns. The 5 layers cast film extrusion pilot line contains 3 extruders, a 5 layer Cloeren combining system (ABCBA & combinations), 1 melt-pump, an 800 mm die width and a corona treatment. The film thickness can be varied from 10 to 350 microns and the max film width at 550 mm. Cast coextrusion film technology enable the encapsulation of recycled polymers (PE or PP) between virgin polymers. Figure 1c: 7-layers blown film extrusion pilot line  The 7 layers blown film pilot line contains 7 extruders, a 150 mm 7-layers Pro-PAK conical die, until 7 layers combining system (ABCDEFG) and a corona treatment. The film thickness can be varied from 30 to 220 microns and the max film width at 550 mm. This technology enables the production of high barrier coextruded film where the recycled polymers (PE or PP) is encapsulated between virgin polymers. Figure 1d below shows the picture of the 5-layers extrusion-coating pilot line 

                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018  
820695- MultiCycle- Part B   Page 89 of 117 
 Figure 1d: 5-layers extrusion-coating / lamination pilot line The 5-layers extrusion-coating/lamination pilot line contains 3 extruders allowing the application of 5 layers in combination with corona treatment and in-line primering. 2) Thin Film Deposition Centre of Excellence Figure 2 below shows the picture of the High Barrier Thin Film Deposition pilot line.  Figure 2: High Barrier Thin Film Deposition Pilot Line The possible coating processes are SiOx (Ceramis process), AlOx, Al and potential further materials. The process uses a vacuum chamber, unwinding and rewinding units. The process starts with a plasma pre-treatment stage where the surface of the substrate film is cleaned and prepared for the coating process. The process uses 2 high voltage electron beam guns to evaporate the silicon oxide materials and build up a cloud above. The film substrate runs over a chilled reel, at ~ -15°C and through the temperature difference the SiOx condensate on the surface of the film. The film thickness can be varied from 6 to 175 microns and the film width from 240 to 715 mm. The applied coating thickness of the SiOx or other materials coating is in nanometre scale. 3) Adhesive Lamination Centre of Excellence Figure 3 below shows the picture of the adhesive lamination pilot line  Figure 3: Adhesive lamination Pilot Line The adhesive lamination pilot line contains: - solvent-based, water-based and solvent-free lamination technologies either by gravure or smooth roll application - Extrusion-lamination (until 5 layers) technology - Radiation curing (UV or EB) lamination technology The maximum lamination width is 600 mm and the maximum speed of the line is at 150 m/min. This pilot line will be used to laminate recycled polymers film combinations type recycled PET/ recycled PE, … 4) Packaging lines competence Centre 

                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018

Figure 4 below shows pictures of the packaging pilot lines  Figure 4: Packaging Pilot Lines  The packaging pilot lines competence centre contains 7 lines including HFFS, VFFS + Deep Drawing, Tray sealer and Vacuum chamber from Multivac. The packaging formats that can be produced are easy pack, pillow pouch, lidding for thermoformed web and lidding for pre-formed tray. Full packaging format made from recycled polymers can be produced and tested as part of the project. 5) Analytical Centre of Excellence The Analytical Centre of Excellence contains: - Product Safety testing (extraction and migration) with chromatography (LC-MS/MS, GC-MS) - Surface Analysis (SEM and LSM) - Spectroscopy (FTIR and micro-Raman) - Thermal Analysis (DSC) - Rheological (DMA, MFI, Rheotens, Cone and Plate Rheometer) - Optical (Polarizing optical microscope, Stereo Microscopy)  - Barrier (OTR, WVTR and CO2 transmission rate) - Mechanical (Puncture resistance, Stiffness, Tear, Leak test, OD, Haze, Transparency, …)   Participant no. 13 Name (short name)/ Country LÖMI GmbH / LOEMI (Germany) Description of the legal entity  The engineer-operated manufacturer LOEMI was established in 1991. Participant no. 18 Name (short name)/ Country Crowdhelix Ltd. (VISION2020: The HORIZONNETWORK LTD.)  (V2020) / UK Description of the legal entity  V2020: Enabling MultiCycle to deliver impact through communication, dissemination and Open Innovation V2020 is a pan-European Open Innovation Network that enables Research Technology Organisations and businesses to collaborate, innovate and grow. The network has more than 350+ member organisations from 41 countries and is present in all EU Member State countries. The network membership is reported to have won more than 2 billion euros of funding under Horizon 2020, highlighting the quality of its membership base.   The network is structured around virtual technology clusters known as Helixes. There are currently 18 live Helixes in areas such as Health, ICT, and Energy etc. The network hosts focussed collaborative events for each Helix each year where the aim is to connect organisations across Europe and promote collaboration and open innovation.    In addition to hosting and running events, V2020 also has its own technology tool called: Crowdhelix. The tool is designed so people and organisations can profile their expertise and capabilities within a Helix area. Crowdhelix is then used to help organisations post opportunities, which are matched to people’s profiles within the platform. Once a match is made the V2020 team then help to facilitate an opportunity so that it then turns into a tangible collaboration Main tasks V2020 will set up a Circular plastics Helix to act as the communication and knowledge exchange platform for this project. This will include all project partners, all relevant stakeholders from the V2020 community (70+ research technological intensive organisations and 250+ SMEs) interested in plastics and the circular economy – expertise, capability, testing, etc. The Helix will also include other aligned projects in the plastics and circular economy domains. The dissemination activities will be split into the following areas: 1: Implementation (events, communication, publications, outreach, access to capabilities, testing etc). 2: Policy; high-level brokerage, regulatory and standardisation requirements. V2020 will establish the Circular Plastics Helix as a virtual technology cluster across the V2020 network and also within the network’s match-making technology tool: Crowdhelix. Crowdhelix will be used as an additional vehicle to profile organisations and people which will enable stakeholders to test, drive through and adopt new innovations that will coming through and/or aligned to the MultiCycle project       V2020 will contribute towards the commercialisation and dissemination activities, which will be channelled through the Circular Plastics Helix. The project’s commercialisation, exploitation and IP strategy will be part of, and integrated into, the Helix activities. It will also help to form and drive new forms of untapped capability and capacity in this area. The Helix will act as the communication and dissemination hub for the project both during and after the project has ended. V2020 will continue to manage the community beyond the end of the project – promoting the project’s outputs and impacts and enabling new forms of collaboration and open innovation across the European Research Area. ISWA works to protect human health and the environment as well as to ensure sustainable resource and waste management. Part of ISWA’s major competencies lie in organizing and participating in  international networking events (annual World Congress, IFAT, ECOMONDO, COPs, and UN-Habitat), conducting educational trainings and workshops on various aspects of waste management (ca. 70+ trainings and events organized in 2017), drafting of technical reports and documents, engaging in developing economies to establish sustainable waste management practices, and the sharing of knowledge and experience in sustainable waste management and climate change mitigation. ISWA has multiple partnerships and MOUs with various international organizations including CCAC, R20, UNFCCC, UNEP, UNIDO, WHO, World Bank, and more. ISWA has an academic journal (Waste Management and Research), a magazine (Waste Management World), a bi-monthly newsletter, and 10 Technical Working Groups that can be used as tools to present, support, and disseminate the activities and results of the project. Main tasks The main tasks foreseen for ISWA in this project are in gathering and providing statistical data regarding the current status of plastic waste recycling in the EU countries where available through ISWA’s network (WP1), provide access to end of life packaging waste to the pilot recycling facility through ISWA members (WP2,4), and communicate and disseminate the project outputs through ISWA’s channels (WP8). ISWA will also be responsible for organizing 3 events with policymakers and help with producing white papers on the project outputs. ISWA has an extensive network worldwide to reach waste management professionals and organizations within its own membership, but also maintains several working relationships with other international organizations through projects and MOU’s which allow ISWA to also reach a wide audience of stakeholders and interested parties within the field of sustainability research and action.  How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project ISWA has an international network of members, stakeholders and contacts globally. Its membership consists of waste management professionals from every continent, as well as waste management companies, and also other national waste management associations. They are joined together in 10 thematic working groups as well as numerous events (including our own yearly World Congress with 1000+ attendees). ISWA has two publications, the Waste Management World magazine and the peer reviewed Waste Management & Research journal, which target respectively the professional waste management community and the research community.  ISWA has participated in H2020 projects before, and is currently also the Communications & Disseminations leader for the project EcoBulk. ISWA acknowledges that plastic recycling has a key role to play in waste management in order to prevent marine litter and make good use of resources. ISWA also maintains a busy calendar of events (70+ events organized in 2017) which include conferences, trainings, study tours and working groups on 10 different sustainability themes. Also, ISWA’s involvement with other EU projects as well as other international agencies allows for a broad view on possible project clustering and synergy opportunities. CV of the persons who will be primarily responsible for carrying out the work Aditi Ramola (Female) is a Technical Project Manager at the ISWA General Secretariat. She graduated with distinction from the Environmental Technology & International Affairs MSc joint programme offered by the Technical University of Vienna and the Diplomatic Academy of Vienna. She received the ‘Best Study Award’ from ARA Altstoff Recycling Austria AG for her exemplary academic performance. She has several years of experience in the private sector and international 

                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018  
820695- MultiCycle- Part B   Page 102 of 117 
organizations such as Caterpillar Inc. and the United Nations Industrial Development Organization where she worked at the Climate Policy and Networks unit of the Department of Energy. Most recently she was involved in the successful completion of the European Commission funded project on Developing an EU Standardised Approach to Vocational Qualifications in Healthcare Waste where she was the lead of the Work Package on Implementation planning and network growth and development. Arne Ragossnig (Male) ISWA Managing Director has completed his PhD-studies in Environmental Engineering – focus: Thermal Utilization of Waste – at the University of Leoben in 2001. After several years being responsible for Sales Controlling and Sales Coordination at the international Austrian plant engineering company VA TECH he became head of the study programme Energy and Environmental Management (MSc.) in 2004 and in addition to that head of the study programme Sustainable Energy Systems (MSc.) in 2006 at University of Applied Science FH Burgenland. As managing director and head of R&D he was responsible for building up research activities at FH Burgenland. In 2012 he became Vice-Rector of FH Burgenland. In 2013 he became self-employed as is managing partner of the engineering company Ecoconsultants. As of 2018 he also is involved in the International Solid Waste Association (ISWA) as managing director. He is lecturer at various universities and associate editor of the scientific ISWA journal Waste Management & Research. Additionally, he is a member of the steering committees of several international conferences such as Recy & DepoTech taking place every second year at University of Leoben. Joachim Quoden (Male) is currently Chair of the ISWA Working Group on Legal Issue. He has extensive experience in packaging waste management, dating from 1992 when he spent 4 months in the German Federal Ministry of Environment working on packaging issues including the German Packaging Ordinance. From 1993 to 2006, Mr Quoden worked with Der Grüne Punkt - Duales System Deutschland GmbH (DSD), where he was appointed head of International Affairs in 2001. Between 2001 and 2013, he also became Secretary General and later Managing Director of PRO EUROPE, the umbrella organisation of 35 packaging recovery organisations. Since 2013, Mr Quoden acts as Managing Director of EXPRA, a new alliance of 26 PRO’s from currently more than 24 countries. Besides the above, Mr Quoden is working since 1995 as independent lawyer in Germany specializing in international EPR legislation, chairperson of ISWA’s Governance & Legal working group, member of the OECD EPR expert group and has served as an expert in ISO global standardisation project SIS/TK 165/AG 10 Packaging and Environment. Björn Appelqvist (Male) is Chair of the ISWA Working Group on Recycling and Waste Minimisation and was the Chair of the ISWA Task Force on Resource Management. He is currently the Head of Department for Waste Management and Site Solutions at Ramboll, having moved here from the City of Denmark where he worked as a Project Manager at the Technical and Environmental Administration of the City of Copenhagen, where he is concerned with waste planning, treatment technologies and development of the city’s waste management system in general. Earlier, he has been working as Development Manager at the solid waste collection company R98 in Copenhagen as well as Development Engineer at the Waste Management Department of the City of Malmö, Sweden. Andreas Bartl (Male) is the Vice-Chair of the ISWA Working Group on Recycling and Waste Minimisation and is currently an Associate Professor and Senior Scientist in the Research Group for Particle Technology, Recycling Technology and Technology Assessment at the Vienna University of Technology. He has several years of experience in fiber technology between textiles, nonwovens and paper. He is the author of several research papers and technical studies. Andreas is currently involved in research projects aiming to recycle textiles which usually consist of various polymers. One approach is to dissolve or decompose certain polymers and make the recycling of the remaining polymer(s) much easier. It is within the scope of the research to use enzymes which, for instance, selectively degrade cellulosic fibers into sugars and make the polyester ready to be recycled. ISWA is a network of experts that is structured in a core group of people at the General Secretariat that are directly employed at ISWA, complemented by a vast number of experts (eg. see the 3 CVs above) that are employed elsewhere and volunteer their time for ISWA activities. ISWA will tap upon these experts that work on a free-lance basis for ISWA and will be appointed as in-house consultants to deliver specific tasks for the project. Profile of the third party: GAW technologies GmbH (GAW) The GAW Group is a group of technology companies operating worldwide for industrial engineering and plant construction . The portfolio includes plant construction, products and industrial services, and serves five essential markets in almost every region of the world: paper, plastics, chemicals, environmental and automotive.  The operational business of the GAW Group is concentrated in the Paper & Pulp, Automotive, Chemical and Plastic Industries, Optoelectronics and Automation Divisions.  A substantial part of the worldwide production of coated paper and board is achieved using processing equipment from GAW. Global market leading automobile manufacturers rely on conveyor technology developed by GAW. Special machinery and recycling units from the GAW companies in the plastics division are successfully established throughout the world. automationX® solutions from our automation division have been steadily promoted in the areas of food, building material, process and infrastructure.  Founded in 1951, the GAW Group is today present in seventeen countries and has more than 550 employees. It achieves an annual turnover of EUR 102 million and maintains a widespread network of production facilities, service and sales offices on every continent in the world.

GAW technologies GmbH,  a supporting pillar of the GAW Group, serves as a guarantor of technological expertise in many industries, especially when it comes to the fully automated preparation and production of pigment, starch, chemicals, coating colour and coating compounds as well as the cleaning and recycling of process wastewater containing pigments. GAW provides process solutions ranging from development, consultancy and engineering, to logistics, supervision and commissioning, as well as training and after sales service. Aditi Ramola (ISWA Technical Director)   Aditi is the current Technical Director at the ISWA General Secretariat. She graduated with distinction from the Environmental Technology & International Affairs MSc joint program offered by the Technical University of Vienna and the Diplomatic Academy of Vienna. She received the ‘Best Study Award’ from ARA Altstoff Recycling Austria AG for her exemplary academic performance. She has several years of experience in the private sector and international organizations such as Caterpillar Inc. and the United Nations Industrial Development Organization where she worked at the Climate Policy and Networks unit of the Department of Energy. Most recently she was involved in the successful completion of the European Commission funded project on Developing an EU Standardized Approach to Vocational Qualifications in Healthcare Waste where she led the Work Package on Implementation planning and network growth and development.  Budget 2 PMs, hourly rate as defined for SME Owners / self-employed persons in Netherlands, € 36.79 Total Budget € 10,521.94   Björn Appelqvist (Chair of ISWA Scientific and Technical Committee)  Björn Appelqvist has worked in the waste management sector for more than 15 years. He was formerly Chair of the ISWA Working Group on Recycling and Waste Minimisation and was the Chair of the ISWA Task Force on Resource Management. He is currently the Head of Department for Waste Management and Site Solutions at Ramboll, having moved from the City of Denmark where he worked as a Project Manager at the Technical and Environmental Administration of the City of Copenhagen, where he is concerned with waste planning, treatment technologies and development of the city’s waste management system in general. Earlier, he had been working as Development Manager at the solid waste collection company R98 in Copenhagen as well as Development Engineer at the Waste Management Department of the City of Malmö, Sweden. Through his involvement in the International Solid Waste Association (ISWA), Björn has addressed issues such as circular economy, resource management and the effects on globalization on the waste management sector on an international level.    Budget 0.5 PMs, hourly rate as defined for SME Owners / self-employed persons in Netherlands, € 36.79 Total Budget € 2,630.49   Andreas Bartl (Vice-Chair of ISWA Working Group on Recycling and Waste Minimisation)  Andreas Bartl is currently an Associate Professor and Senior Scientist in the Research Group for Particle Technology, Recycling Technology and Technology Assessment at the Vienna University of Technology. He has several years of experience in fiber technology between textiles, nonwovens and paper. He is the author of several research papers and technical studies.  Andreas is currently involved in research projects aiming to recycle textiles which usually consist of various polymers.  One approach is to dissolve or decompose certain polymers and make the recycling of the remaining polymer(s) much easier. It is within the scope of the research to use enzymes which, for instance, selectively degrade cellulosic fibers into sugars and make the polyester ready to be recycled. 5: Ethics and Security 5.1 Ethics During the preparation of this project, in keeping with the required Ethics Appraisal Procedure, an Ethics Self-assessment was performed with the completion of the Ethical Issues Table, and this project does not involve Ethics issues. It is not expected that personal data will be handled but shall it be necessary at any point, it would be done in compliance with the GDPR to come into force in May 2018 also keeping with H2020 guidelines in terms of recruitment, informed consent, data storage, protection and destruction procedures (no personal information will be collected during surveys, which will be anonymous, not involve minors nor any audio or video recording). Although the self-assessment identified no ethics issues arising from the actual workplan itself, it is worthy of comment the measures that we are taking during the project work plan to address and mitigate any concerns that could indeed appear in the future:  Regulatory activities have been incorporated from the outset of the project with the intention of gathering data to fuel into a further safe and compliant development phase. In terms of product, we will deal with food safety regulations for packaging but also with CE and safety compliance of the MultiCycle pilot plant (ATEX Directive 2014/34/EU (Annex IX) or IECEx Scheme).   The appropriate health and safety procedures conforming to relevant local/national guidelines/legislation will be followed by staff involved in this project. In this sense, all partners follow recognised hygiene and safety rules, including chemical regulations such as REACH, which polymers are exempt from but will be duly followed when dealing with any other chemical.   The use of LCA, which identifies environmental as well as health impacts, can help identify where the maximum impact could occur providing the opportunity for process or material modifications to minimise these impacts.  Finally measures related to responsible research & innovation, spread as relevant along the work plan, are overseen in WP10. All in all, the developed processes will provide a significant environmental improvement (lowering land filling, depletion of fossil resources) resulting in very pure polymers that can be used in packaging and automotive thereby responding to growing consumers desires to make more responsible choices. Furthermore, in terms of end of life, as seen, currently only a minor share of the plastic is recycled and a far too high proportion is landfilled which, in the end, leads to direct and indirect pollution for example when plastics are blown away from their place of disposal. In fact, whereas no plastic was ever 
                         CE-SPIRE-10-2018  
820695- MultiCycle- Part B   Page 113 of 117 
designed to be disposed off in the environment, our lands and oceans are filled with millions of tonnes of plastics that will unfortunately last for hundred years, creating an ever mounting problem. So there is no doubt that developing economically profitable processes and schemes for recycling plastic-based materials will promote their collection so on the long term potentially reducing pollution by plastics. All in all, how ethical is it to continue jeopardising our future generation’s ability to access resources?
5.2 Security  The project will involve NO: • activities or results raising security issues • 'EU-classified information' as background or results.
